import torch
import torch.nn as nn

class Model(nn.Module):
    """
    Performs a standard 2D convolution operation with asymmetric input and kernel sizes.

    Args:
        in_channels (int): Number of channels in the input tensor.
        out_channels (int): Number of channels produced by the convolution.
        kernel_size (tuple): Tuple of two integers representing the height and width of the convolution kernel.
        stride (tuple, optional): Tuple of two integers representing the stride in the height and width dimensions. Defaults to (1, 1).
        padding (tuple, optional): Tuple of two integers representing the padding in the height and width dimensions. Defaults to (0, 0).
        dilation (tuple, optional): Tuple of two integers representing the dilation in the height and width dimensions. Defaults to (1, 1).
        groups (int, optional): Number of blocked connections from input channels to output channels. Defaults to 1.
        bias (bool, optional): If `True`, adds a learnable bias to the output. Defaults to `False`.
    """
    def __init__(self, in_channels: int, out_channels: int, kernel_size: tuple, stride: tuple = (1, 1), padding: tuple = (0, 0), dilation: tuple = (1, 1), groups: int = 1, bias: bool = False):
        super(Model, self).__init__()
        self.conv2d = nn.Conv2d(in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size, stride=stride, padding=padding, dilation=dilation, groups=groups, bias=bias)
        
    def forward(self, x: torch.Tensor) -> torch.Tensor:
        """
        Performs the 2D convolution.

        Args:
            x (torch.Tensor): Input tensor of shape (batch_size, in_channels, height, width).

        Returns:
            torch.Tensor: Output tensor of shape (batch_size, out_channels, height_out, width_out).
        """
        return self.conv2d(x)

# Test code
batch_size = 8
in_channels = 64
out_channels = 128
kernel_size = (5, 7)
height = 512
width = 256

def get_inputs():
    x = torch.rand(batch_size, in_channels, height, width)
    return [x]

def get_init_inputs():
    return [in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size]  # Provide in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size for initialization

Implicit GEMM avoids this. For implicit GEMM, for each output tile (say 64x128 where 64 is spatial positions and 128 is output channels), we load the corresponding input values on-the-fly. For block_M=64 spatial positions and block_N=128 output channels: - 64 spatial positions correspond to some (b, oh, ow) coordinates - For each of the 64 positions, we need K=2240 input values (across in_channels, kh, kw) - For each of the 128 output channels, we need K=2240 weight values But wait, for implicit GEMM, we're computing a block of C where C = A * B: - A is M×K where M is spatial, K is in_channels*kh*kw - B is K×N where N is out_channels - C is M×N In implicit GEMM for convolutions: - To compute a tile of C (spatial tile × output channels), we need corresponding elements from A and B - But getting elements from A requires gathering from the input image based on (b, oh, ow, kh, kw) So for each k step (e.g., k_sliced into chunks), we load: - For A: for each spatial position in the tile, we need one value from input per k. To maximize coalescing, we should map k such that when threads load A in parallel, they access contiguous memory. Let me design a kernel: ```cuda template<int BLOCK_M, int BLOCK_N, int BLOCK_K> __global__ void conv_implicit_gemm( const float* input, const float* weight, float* output, int batch, int in_c, int out_c, int h, int w, int out_h, int out_w, int kh, int kw, int stride_h, int stride_w, int pad_h, int pad_w) { // Each block computes BLOCK_M spatial positions × BLOCK_N output channels // We iterate over K in BLOCK_K chunks int block_m = blockIdx.x; // spatial tile int block_n = blockIdx.y; // output channel tile int b = blockIdx.z; // batch // ... compute base spatial position from block_m // ... load weight tile into shared memory // ... for each k chunk, load input values into shared memory // ... compute dot products using registers } ``` One issue with implicit GEMM is that consecutive spatial positions in the M dimension might not correspond to contiguous memory in the input. Actually, for a 5x7 kernel, two output positions that are close in output space will need overlapping input regions, so there IS locality. In fact, for consecutive ow values, the input windows overlap by 6 pixels. This is great for shared memory caching! If we tile spatially, e.g., a tile of 8x8 output positions, the corresponding input region is (8+4) x (8+6) = 12x14. This is small and can fit in shared memory. This suggests a **direct convolution with shared memory tiling** approach: 1. Divide the output into tiles (e.g., 8x8 spatial tiles, or 16x4, etc.) 2. Each thread block processes one tile for a subset of output channels 3. Load the corresponding input region into shared memory 4. Load weights into shared memory or registers 5. Compute convolution for each output channel Let's calculate shared memory requirements for an input tile: For tile size (TH, TW) = (8, 8): Input region: (8+4) x (8+6) x 64 channels = 12 x 14 x 64 floats = 10,752 floats = 43 KB For shared memory per SM = 228 KB, we could theoretically have 5 such blocks per SM, but we're limited by other resources. If we also load weights: say we process 32 output channels at a time. Weights: 32 x 64 x 5 x 7 = 71,680 floats = 286 KB. That's too much for shared memory! So we need to tile over input channels too. Actually, the standard approach is to NOT load the entire window into registers at once, but to iterate through the kernel dimensions with the weights: ``` for ic = 0..63: load input tile for this ic into SMEM for kh = 0..4: for kw = 0..6: load weight[oc0:oc7, ic, kh, kw] into SMEM or registers for each thread (tx, ty): inp = smem_input[ty+kh, tx+kw] for oci = 0..7: acc[oci] += inp * weight[oci] ``` This way, for each (ic, kh, kw), there are 8 FMAs, and we can unroll the kh, kw loops. Let me write the kernel: ```python kernel_code = ''' import torch from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline cuda_source = """ #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <cuda_fp16.h> #define TILE_H 16 #define TILE_W 16 #define OC_PER_BLOCK 32 #define IC_PER_BLOCK 8 #define KH 5 #define KW 7 __global__ void conv2d_direct_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ weight, float* __restrict__ output, int batch, int in_c, int out_c, int h, int w, int out_h, int out_w) { int b = blockIdx.z; ic_block < in_c / IC_PER_BLOCK; ic_block++) { // Load input tile for this ic_block into smem int in_row = tid / (TILE_W + KW - 1); int in_col = tid % (TILE_W + KW - 1); int in_stride = blockDim.x * blockDim.y; // 256 for (int idx = tid; idx < IC_PER_BLOCK * (TILE_H + KH - 1) * (TILE_W + KW - 1); idx += in_stride) { int tmp = idx; int ici = tmp / ((TILE_H + KH - 1) * (TILE_W + KW - 1)); tmp %= (TILE_H + KH - 1) * (TILE_W + KW - 1); int ih_local = tmp / (TILE_W + KW - 1); int iw_local = tmp % (TILE_W + KW - 1); int global_ih = tile_oh + ih_local; int global_iw = tile_ow + iw_local; float val = 0.0f; if (global_ih < h && global_iw < w) { val = input[((b * in_c + (ic_block * IC_PER_BLOCK + ici)) * h + global_ih) * w + global_iw]; int kh = tmp / KW; int kw = tmp % KW; // oc_block is blockIdx.z ? No, we need to handle oc_block separately. // For simplicity, let's say each block handles all OC_PER_BLOCK for one oc_block. // oc_block is stored separately or derived from blockIdx. } ``` Wait, I realize I forgot to handle the output channel partitioning! Now let me sketch the kernel: ```cuda __global__ void conv2d_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ weight_blocked, float* __restrict__ output, int batch, int in_c, int out_c, int h, int w, int out_h, int out_w) { const int TILE_H = 16; const int TILE_W = 16; const int OC_PER_BLOCK = 64; const int IC_PER_BLOCK = 4; int b = blockIdx.z / (out_c / OC_PER_BLOCK); int oc_block = blockIdx.z % (out_c / OC_PER_BLOCK); int oc_start = oc_block * OC_PER_BLOCK; int tile_oh = blockIdx.y * TILE_H; int tile_ow = blockIdx.x * TILE_W; int local_ow = threadIdx.x; int local_oh = threadIdx.y; int oh = tile_oh + local_oh; int ow = tile_ow + local_ow; __shared__ float smem_input[IC_PER_BLOCK][TILE_H + KH - 1][TILE_W + KW - 1]; __shared__ float smem_weight[OC_PER_BLOCK][IC_PER_BLOCK][KH][KW]; float acc[OC_PER_BLOCK]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < OC_PER_BLOCK; i++) { acc[i] = 0.0f; } for (int ic_block = 0; ic_block < in_c / IC_PER_BLOCK; ic_block++) { // Cooperative load of input tile int total_input = IC_PER_BLOCK * (TILE_H + KH - 1) * (TILE_W + KW - 1); for (int idx = threadIdx.y * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; idx < total_input; idx += blockDim.x * blockDim.y) { int tmp = idx; int ici = tmp / ((TILE_H + KH - 1) * (TILE_W + KW - 1)); tmp %= ((TILE_H + KH - 1) * (TILE_W + KW - 1)); int ih_local = tmp / (TILE_W + KW - 1); int iw_local = tmp % (TILE_W + KW - 1); int global_ih = tile_oh + ih_local; int global_iw = tile_ow + iw_local; float val = 0.0f; if (global_ih < h && global_iw < w) { val = input[((b * in_c + (ic_block * IC_PER_BLOCK + ici)) * h + global_ih) * w + global_iw]; } smem_input[ici][ih_local][iw_local] = val; } // Cooperative load of weights // weight_blocked layout: [oc_block, ic_block, kh, kw, OC_PER_BLOCK, IC_PER_BLOCK] int total_weight = OC_PER_BLOCK * IC_PER_BLOCK * KH * KW; for (int idx = threadIdx.y * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; idx < total_weight; idx += blockDim.x * blockDim.y) { int tmp = idx; int oci = tmp / (IC_PER_BLOCK * KH * KW); tmp %= (IC_PER_BLOCK * KH * KW); int ici = tmp / (KH * KW); tmp %= (KH * KW); int kh = tmp / KW; int kw = tmp % KW; float val = weight_blocked[((oc_block * (in_c / IC_PER_BLOCK) + ic_block) * KH * KW * OC_PER_BLOCK * IC_PER_BLOCK + (kh * KW + kw) * OC_PER_BLOCK * IC_PER_BLOCK + oci * IC_PER_BLOCK + ici)]; smem_weight[oci][ici][kh][kw] = val; } __syncthreads(); // Compute #pragma unroll for (int ici = 0; ici < IC_PER_BLOCK; ici++) { #pragma unroll for (int kh = 0; kh < KH; kh++) { #pragma unroll for (int kw = 0; kw < KW; kw++) { float in_val = smem_input[ici][local_oh + kh][local_ow + kw]; #pragma unroll for (int oci = 0; oci < OC_PER_BLOCK; oci++) { acc[oci] += in_val * smem_weight[oci][ici][kh][kw]; } } } } __syncthreads(); } // Write output if (oh < out_h && ow < out_w) { #pragma unroll for (int oci = 0; oci < OC_PER_BLOCK; oci++) { int global_oc = oc_start + oci; output[((b * out_c + global_oc) * out_h + oh) * out_w + ow] = acc[oci]; } } } ``` I need to be careful about: 1. `local_oh + kh` and `local_ow + kw` could exceed shared memory bounds for threads near the boundary of the tile. 1) * (TILE_W + KW - 1);\n for (int idx = tid; idx < total_input; idx += blockDim.x * blockDim.y) {\n int ih_local = idx / (TILE_W + KW - 1);\n int iw_local = idx % (TILE_W + KW - 1);\n int global_ih = tile_oh + ih_local;\n int global_iw = tile_ow + iw_local;\n float val = 0.0f;\n if (global_ih < h && global_iw < w) {\n val = input[((b * in_c + ic) * h + global_ih) * w + global_iw];\n }\n smem_input[ih_local][iw_local] = val;\n }\n \n int total_weight = OC_BLOCK * KH * KW;\n for (int idx = tid; idx < total_weight; idx += blockDim.x * blockDim.y) {\n int oci = idx / (KH * KW);\n int tmp = idx % (KH * KW);\n int kh = tmp / KW;\n int kw = tmp % KW;\n int global_oc = oc_start + oci;\n float val = weight[((global_oc * in_c + ic) * KH + kh) * KW + kw];\n smem_weight[oci][kh][kw] = val;\n }\n \n __syncthreads();\n \n if (oh < out_h && ow < out_w) {\n #pragma unroll\n for (int kh = 0; kh < KH; kh++) {\n #pragma unroll\n for (int kw = 0; kw < KW; kw++) {\n float in_val = smem_input[local_oh + kh][local_ow + kw];\n #pragma unroll\n for (int oci = 0; oci < OC_BLOCK; oci++) {\n acc[oci] += in_val * smem_weight[oci][kh][kw];\n }\n }\n }\n }\n \n __syncthreads();\n }\n \n if (oh < out_h && ow < out_w) {\n #pragma unroll\n for (int oci = 0; oci < OC_BLOCK; oci++) {\n int global_oc = oc_start + oci;\n output[((b * out_c + global_oc) * out_h + oh) * out_w + ow] = acc[oci];\n }\n }\n}\n\ntorch::Tensor conv2d_forward(\n torch::Tensor input,\n torch::Tensor weight,\n int64_t batch, int64_t in_c, int64_t out_c,\n int64_t h, int64_t w, int64_t out_h, int64_t out_w) {\n \n auto output = torch::empty({batch, out_c, out_h, out_w}, input.options());\n \n dim3 block(TILE_W, TILE_H);\n dim3 grid(\n (out_w + TILE_W - 1) / TILE_W,\n (out_h + TILE_H - 1) / TILE_H,\n batch * (out_c / OC_BLOCK)\n );\n \n conv2d_kernel<<<grid, block>>>(\n input.data_ptr<float>(),\n weight.data_ptr<float>(),\n output.data_ptr<float>(),\n batch, in_c, out_c,\n h, w, out_h, out_w\n );\n \n return output;\n}\n\"\"\"\n\nconv2d_module = load_inline(\n name=\"conv2d_inline\",\n cpp_sources=cpp_source,\n cuda_sources=cuda_source,\n functions=[\"conv2d_forward\"],\n extra_cuda_cflags=[\"-O3\", \"--use_fast_math\"],\n)\n\nclass ModelNew(torch.nn.Module):\n def __init__(self, in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size, stride=(1, 1), padding=(0, 0), dilation=(1, 1), groups=1, bias=False):\n super(ModelNew, self).__init__()\n self.in_channels = in_channels\n self.out_channels = out_channels\n self.kernel_size = kernel_size\n self.stride = stride\n self.padding = padding\n self.dilation = dilation\n self.groups = groups\n \n self.weight = torch.nn.Parameter(torch.empty(out_channels, in_channels, kernel_size[0], kernel_size[1]))\n if bias:\n self.bias = torch.nn.Parameter(torch.empty(out_channels))\n else:\n self.register_parameter('bias', None)\n \n torch.nn.init.kaiming_uniform_(self.weight, a=math.sqrt(5))\n if self.bias is not None:\n fan_in, _ = torch.nn.init._calculate_fan_in_and_fan_out(self.weight)\n bound = 1 / math.sqrt(fan_in)\n torch.nn.init.uniform_(self.bias, -bound, bound)\n \n def forward(self, x):\n batch = x.size(0)\n h = x.size(2)\n w = x.size(3)\n out_h = (h + 2 * self.padding[0] - self.dilation[0] * (self.kernel_size[0] - 1) - 1) // self.stride[0] + 1\n out_w = (w + 2 * self.padding[1] - self.dilation[1] * (self.kernel_size[1] - 1) - 1) // self.stride[1] + 1\n \n if self.padding[0] > 0 or self.padding[1] > 0:\n x = torch.nn.functional.pad(x, (self.padding[1], self.padding[1], self.padding[0], self.padding[0]))\n h = x.size(2)\n w = x.size(3)\n \n return conv2d_module.conv2d_forward(\n x, self.weight,\n batch, self.in_channels, self.out_channels,\n h, w, out_h, out_w\n )\n" }

1) * (TILE_W + KW - 1);\n for (int idx = tid; idx < total_input; idx += blockDim.x * blockDim.y) {\n int ih_local = idx / (TILE_W + KW - 1);\n int iw_local = idx % (TILE_W + KW - 1);\n int global_ih = tile_oh + ih_local;\n int global_iw = tile_ow + iw_local;\n float val = 0.0f;\n if (global_ih < h && global_iw < w) {\n val = input[((b * in_c + ic) * h + global_ih) * w + global_iw];\n }\n smem_input[ih_local][iw_local] = val;\n }\n \n int total_weight = OC_BLOCK * KH * KW;\n for (int idx = tid; idx < total_weight; idx += blockDim.x * blockDim.y) {\n int oci = idx / (KH * KW);\n int tmp = idx % (KH * KW);\n int kh = tmp / KW;\n int kw = tmp % KW;\n int global_oc = oc_start + oci;\n float val = weight[((global_oc * in_c + ic) * KH + kh) * KW + kw];\n smem_weight[oci][kh][kw] = val;\n }\n \n __syncthreads();\n \n if (oh < out_h && ow < out_w) {\n #pragma unroll\n for (int kh = 0; kh < KH; kh++) {\n #pragma unroll\n for (int kw = 0; kw < KW; kw++) {\n float in_val = smem_input[local_oh + kh][local_ow + kw];\n #pragma unroll\n for (int oci = 0; oci < OC_BLOCK; oci++) {\n acc[oci] += in_val * smem_weight[oci][kh][kw];\n }\n }\n }\n }\n \n __syncthreads();\n }\n \n if (oh < out_h && ow < out_w) {\n #pragma unroll\n for (int oci = 0; oci < OC_BLOCK; oci++) {\n int global_oc = oc_start + oci;\n output[((b * out_c + global_oc) * out_h + oh) * out_w + ow] = acc[oci];\n }\n }\n}\n\ntorch::Tensor conv2d_forward(\n torch::Tensor input,\n torch::Tensor weight,\n int64_t batch, int64_t in_c, int64_t out_c,\n int64_t h, int64_t w, int64_t out_h, int64_t out_w) {\n \n auto output = torch::empty({batch, out_c, out_h, out_w}, input.options());\n \n dim3 block(TILE_W, TILE_H);\n dim3 grid(\n (out_w + TILE_W - Let's structure the kernel: - Block dimensions: (16, 16, 1) threads. - Each block handles a 16x16 spatial tile and a chunk of `OC` (e.g., 64). - Grid: `(out_w/16, out_h/16, batch * ceil(out_c/64))`. - Each thread computes one spatial pixel (`oh`, `ow`) and all 64 output channels in that chunk. - For each `ic`: - Load a tile of input into shared memory (including halo). - For each `kh`, `kw`, `oci` (0..63): - acc[oci] += smem_input[...] * weight[...]; - If we keep `acc[64]` in registers, that's 64 floats = 256 bytes = 64 registers just for accumulation. Let's try to make a robust generic kernel without shared memory for weights, but with shared memory for input. ```cpp __global__ void conv2d_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ weight, float* __restrict__ output, int batch, int in_c, int out_c, int h, int w, int out_h, int out_w, int kh, int kw) { // Tile size const int TILE_H = 16; const int TILE_W = 16; const int OC_BLOCK = 32; int b = blockIdx.z / ((out_c + OC_BLOCK - 1) / OC_BLOCK); int oc_block = blockIdx.z % ((out_c + OC_BLOCK - 1) / OC_BLOCK); int oc_start = oc_block * OC_BLOCK; int oc_end = min(oc_start + OC_BLOCK, out_c); int oc_count = oc_end - oc_start; int tile_oh = blockIdx.y * TILE_H; int tile_ow = blockIdx.x * TILE_W; int local_ow = threadIdx.x; int local_oh = threadIdx.y; int tid = threadIdx.y * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; int oh = tile_oh + local_oh; int ow = tile_ow + local_ow; extern __shared__ float smem[]; // or static if max size known // smem size: (TILE_H + kh - 1) * (TILE_W + kw - 1) } ``` Static shared memory with dynamic size is only possible via dynamic allocation or just use a large static array. Let's use a static array big enough: `__shared__ float smem_input[48][48];` (supports up to tile + kernel where tile could be up to 32 and kernel up to 16). The size is `(tile_h + kh - 1) * (tile_w + kw - 1) * sizeof(float)`. Since `kh, kw` are passed as args (or constexpr), we can compute at host side. Using dynamic shared memory is cleaner. Let's do that. And for weights, we load from global memory. Design of the generic kernel: ```cpp __global__ void conv2d_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ weight, float* __restrict__ output, int batch, int in_c, int out_c, int h, int w, int out_h, int out_w, int kh, int kw) { const int TILE_H = 16; const int TILE_W = 16; int b = blockIdx.z / ((out_c + 31) / 32); int oc_block = blockIdx.z % ((out_c + 31) / 32); int oc_start = oc_block * 32; int oc_end = min(oc_start + 32, out_c); int oc_count = oc_end - oc_start; int tile_oh = blockIdx.y * TILE_H; int tile_ow = blockIdx.x * TILE_W; int local_ow = threadIdx.x; int local_oh = threadIdx.y; int tid = threadIdx.y * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; int oh = tile_oh + local_oh; int ow = tile_ow + local_ow; extern __shared__ float smem[]; int smem_h = TILE_H + kh - 1; int smem_w = TILE_W + kw - 1; float acc[32]; // max 32 output channels per thread for (int i = 0; i < 32; i++) acc[i] = 0.0f; for (int ic = 0; ic < in_c; ic++) { // load input tile int total = smem_h * smem_w; for (int idx = tid; idx < total; idx += blockDim.x * blockDim.y) { int ih_local = idx / smem_w; int iw_local = idx % smem_w; int global_ih = tile_oh + ih_local; int global_iw = tile_ow + iw_local; float val = 0.0f; if (global_ih < h && global_iw < w) { val = input[((b * in_c + ic) * h + global_ih) * w + global_iw]; } smem[ih_local * smem_w + iw_local] = val; } __syncthreads(); if (oh < out_h && ow < out_w) { for (int k_h = 0; k_h < kh; k_h++) { for (int k_w = 0; k_w < kw; k_w++) { float in_val = smem[(local_oh + k_h) * smem_w + (local_ow + k_w)]; for (int oci = 0; oci < oc_count; oci++) { int global_oc = oc_start + oci; float w_val = weight[((global_oc * in_c + ic) * kh + k_h) * kw + k_w]; acc[oci] += in_val * w_val; } } } } __syncthreads(); } if (oh < out_h && ow < out_w) { for (int oci = 0; oci < oc_count; oci++) { int global_oc = oc_start + oci; output[((b * out_c + global_oc) * out_h + oh) * out_w + ow] = acc[oci]; } } } ``` Register usage: `acc[32]` = 32 registers. We can just treat everything as row-major and transpose via cublas parameters. Specifically: - `im2col` kernel: writes a matrix `col` of shape `[N, C*KH*KW, out_h, out_w]` or flatten to `[N*out_h*out_w, C*KH*KW]`. - Weight matrix `W` of shape `[out_c, C*KH*KW]` (we can reshape weight). - We want output `Y` of shape `[N, out_c, out_h*out_w]`. - We can do: `Y = X_col @ W.T` in terms of shapes: - X_col: [N*out_h*out_w, C*KH*KW] - W: [out_c, C*KH*KW] - Y: [N*out_h*out_w, out_c] If we treat matrices as column-major for cublas: - A = W^T: [C*KH*KW, out_c] - B = X_col^T: [C*KH*KW, N*out_h*out_w] - C = Y^T: [out_c, N*out_h*out_w] - Then C = A^T * B? Actually, cublas does C = alpha * op(A) * op(B) + beta * C. We want C (col-major) [out_c, N*out_h*out_w] = W (row-major [out_c, C*KH*KW]) * X_col (row-major [N*out_h*out_w, C*KH*KW])^T ? Hmm. Let's just use row-major logic: C_row = A_row * B_row. We can map to cublas column-major using transposes: C_col_major = B_col_major * A_col_major. If A_row = W of shape [M=oc, K=ic*kh*kw], then A_col_major is its transpose of shape [K, M]. If B_row = X_col of shape [N=batch*oh*ow, K=ic*kh*kw], then B_col_major is its transpose of shape [K, N]. Actually, `load_inline` does: 1. Writes source files. 2. Runs `ninja` to build. 3. Calls `_import_module_from_library(name, build_directory, True)`. 4. In `_import_module_from_library`, it uses `imp.load_module` or `importlib.util.spec_from_file_location` to load the .so file. This stores `k` as the column index, `n` as the row index. So it's NxK column-major. Then cublas sees B = X_col as column-major [rows=N, cols=K] with `opB = N`. op(B) is NxK. We need KxN. It is stored as `C[m][n] -> mem[m + n*M]`. Can we interpret this directly as our output? Our desired output shape is `[batch, out_c, out_h, out_w]`. For a single batch, we can view it as `[out_c, out_h*out_w]`. This is `M x N` in row-major (since out_c is the slowest varying dim?). In PyTorch, tensor `y[n, c, h, w]` is stored with strides: n_stride = c*h*w, c_stride = h*w, h_stride = w, w_stride = 1. So for fixed n, `y[c, h, w]` has c as the outermost dimension, then h, then w. If we flatten h and w into P = h*w, then for fixed n, `y[c, p]` is stored with stride P between c. So it's essentially M x N row-major! (Since element (c, p) is at offset c*P + p). cublas writes column-major MxN: element (c, p) is at offset c + p*M. This is NOT our PyTorch layout. So we need to transpose the result. Options: 1. Have cublas compute C^T = B * A (with appropriate ops) to get the output in row-major. - We want `C_row = MxN` row-major = `(NxM column-major)^T`. - cublas computes `C_col = A' * B'`. We want `C_col` to be `NxM` column-major (which is `MxN` row-major). - So we need `C_col` dimensions N x M. - `A'` should be `N x K`, `B'` should be `K x M`. - We have B = X_col in column-major NxK. If `op(B)=N`, then `op(B)=NxK`. - We have A = W in column-major KxM. If `op(A)=N`, then `op(A)=KxM`. - Then `C = op(B) * op(A) = NxK * KxM = NxM` column-major. That's what we want! - So call `cublasSgemm(handle, CUBLAS_OP_N, CUBLAS_OP_N, N, M, K, &alpha, B, N, A, K, &beta, C, N)`. - Here A pointer is W, B pointer is X_col, C pointer is output. - A is W in column-major KxM. `lda = K`? Let's do that, with dynamic smem size. kernel design: ```cpp __global__ void conv2d_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ weight, float* __restrict__ output, int batch, int in_c, int out_c, int h, int w, int out_h, int out_w, int kh, int kw) { const int TILE_H = 16; const int TILE_W = 16; const int OC_BLOCK = 32; int b = blockIdx.z / ((out_c + OC_BLOCK - 1) / OC_BLOCK); int oc_block = blockIdx.z % ((out_c + OC_BLOCK - 1) / OC_BLOCK); int oc_start = oc_block * OC_BLOCK; int oc_end = min(oc_start + OC_BLOCK, out_c); int oc_count = oc_end - oc_start; int tile_oh = blockIdx.y * TILE_H; int tile_ow = blockIdx.x * TILE_W; int local_ow = threadIdx.x; int local_oh = threadIdx.y; int tid = threadIdx.y * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; int oh = tile_oh + local_oh; int ow = tile_ow + local_ow; extern __shared__ float smem[]; int smem_h = TILE_H + kh - 1; int smem_w = TILE_W + kw - 1; // smem layout: smem_h * smem_w floats // We'll keep acc in registers. Max OC_BLOCK = 32. #define MAX_OC_BLOCK 32 float acc[MAX_OC_BLOCK]; for (int i = 0; i < oc_count; i++) acc[i] = 0.0f; for (int ic = 0; ic < in_c; ic++) { // Load input tile int total = smem_h * smem_w; for (int idx = tid; idx < total; idx += blockDim.x * blockDim.y) { int ih_local = idx / smem_w; int iw_local = idx % smem_w; int global_ih = tile_oh + ih_local; int global_iw = tile_ow + iw_local; float val = 0.0f; if (global_ih < h && global_iw < w) { val = input[((b * in_c + ic) * h + global_ih) * w + global_iw]; } smem[ih_local * smem_w + iw_local] = val; } __syncthreads(); if (oh < out_h && ow < out_w) { for (int k_h = 0; k_h < kh; k_h++) { for (int k_w = 0; k_w < kw; k_w++) { float in_val = smem[(local_oh + k_h) * smem_w + (local_ow + k_w)]; // We need to load weights for each oc in this block. // The weight pointer for (global_oc, ic, k_h, k_w) is: // weight[((global_oc * in_c + ic) * kh + k_h) * kw + k_w] // global_oc = oc_start + oci. for (int oci = 0; oci < oc_count; oci++) { int global_oc = oc_start + oci; float w_val = weight[((global_oc * in_c + ic) * kh + k_h) * kw + k_w]; acc[oci] += in_val * w_val; } } } } __syncthreads(); } if (oh < out_h && ow < out_w) { for (int oci = 0; oci < oc_count; oci++) { int global_oc = oc_start + oci; output[((b * out_c + global_oc) * out_h + oh) * out_w + ow] = acc[oci]; } } } ``` Launch: `smem_size = smem_h * smem_w * sizeof(float)` Grid: `dim3 grid((out_w + TILE_W - 1) / TILE_W, (out_h + TILE_H - 1) / TILE_H, batch * ((out_c + OC_BLOCK - 1) / OC_BLOCK))` This kernel is generic for any kh, kw (up to what fits in shared memory, which is large: if TILE_H=16, TILE_W=16, max kh+kw such that (16+kh-1)*(16+kw-1) fits in ~200KB. That's huge. For kh=7,kw=7: 22*22=484 floats = 2KB. Fine. Performance: each thread does `in_c * kh * kw * oc_count` FMAs. For test: 64 * 5 * 7 * 32 = 71,680 FMAs per thread. Wow, that's a lot. With 256 threads per block, that's 18.3M FMAs per block. At 67 TFLOPS, that's plenty of compute. Wait, but each block only handles 16x16 spatial pixels. Total blocks = 8*4*16*32 = 16384. Updated kernel with weight in smem: ```cpp extern __shared__ float smem[]; // Layout: smem_input (smem_h * smem_w), then smem_weight (OC_BLOCK * kh * kw) // But smem_h and smem_w depend on kh and kw. We can just index manually. float* smem_input = smem; float* smem_weight = smem + smem_h * smem_w; ``` However, `smem_weight` size is `OC_BLOCK * kh * kw`. For `oc_count` (<=32) and kh=5, kw=7, it's 1120 floats = 4.5KB. Total smem per block = ~2KB (input) + ~4.5KB = ~6.5KB. Very small. Load weights for this `ic`: ```cpp int weight_total = oc_count * kh * kw; for (int idx = tid; idx < weight_total; idx += blockDim.x * blockDim.y) { int oci = idx / (kh * kw); int tmp = idx % (kh * kw); int k_h = tmp / kw; int k_w = tmp % kw; int global_oc = oc_start + oci; smem_weight[oci * kh * kw + tmp] = weight[((global_oc * in_c + ic) * kh + k_h) * kw + k_w]; } ``` Note: `tmp` uniquely identifies `(k_h, k_w)` since `tmp = k_h * kw + k_w`. So `smem_weight[oci * kh * kw + k_h * kw + k_w]`. Then in the compute loop: ```cpp for (int k_h = 0; k_h < kh; k_h++) { for (int k_w = 0; k_w < kw; k_w++) { float in_val = smem_input[(local_oh + k_h) * smem_w + (local_ow + k_w)]; for (int oci = 0; oci < oc_count; oci++) { acc[oci] += in_val * smem_weight[oci * kh * kw + k_h * kw + k_w]; } } } ``` Now the inner loop is all shared memory and registers. This is much faster. Let's use this. Let's write the code with this design and test. If it compiles correctly, we can benchmark. I'll write the kernel using `extern __shared__ float smem[];`. Actually, we can handle groups easily in the host wrapper: - For each group g: - Input slice: `x[:, g*in_c_per_group : (g+1)*in_c_per_group, :, :]` - Weight slice: `weight[g*out_c_per_group : (g+1)*out_c_per_group, :, :, :]` - Call our kernel on these slices. - Concatenate outputs. This is efficient and avoids writing group logic in CUDA. But requires extra memory views. Since the test uses groups=1, this is fine. Let's write a wrapper that handles groups in Python, and passes `stride`, `padding`, `dilation` to the kernel. We'll pre-pad in Python to simplify the kernel. So Python `forward`: ```python def forward(self, x): batch = x.size(0) h, w = x.size(2), x.size(3) # Compute output dims out_h = (h + 2*pad_h - dilation_h*(kh-1) - 1) // stride_h + 1 out_w = (w + 2*pad_w - dilation_w*(kw-1) - 1) // stride_w + 1 # Pre-pad if self.padding[0] > 0 or self.padding[1] > 0: x = F.pad(x, (pad_w, pad_w, pad_h, pad_h)) h, w = x.size(2), x.size(3) out = torch.empty(batch, self.out_channels, out_h, out_w, dtype=x.dtype, device=x.device) in_c_per_group = self.in_channels // self.groups out_c_per_group = self.out_channels // self.groups for g in range(self.groups): x_g = x[:, g*in_c_per_group:(g+1)*in_c_per_group] w_g = self.weight[g*out_c_per_group:(g+1)*out_c_per_group] out_g = conv2d_module.conv2d_forward( x_g, w_g, batch, in_c_per_group, out_c_per_group, h, w, out_h, out_w, self.kernel_size[0], self.kernel_size[1], self.stride[0], self.stride[1], self.dilation[0], self.dilation[1] ) out[:, g*out_c_per_group:(g+1)*out_c_per_group] = out_g if self.bias is not None: out += self.bias.view(1, -1, 1, 1) return out ``` This is correct and handles groups. It won't trigger static check because we don't call `nn.Conv2d`. But it does call `torch.empty` and slicing, which is fine. For `bias`, we add it after. The test uses bias=False, but the constructor supports it. Now let's write the CUDA kernel. It needs to accept `stride_h, stride_w, dilation_h, dilation_w`. ```cpp __global__ void conv2d_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ weight, int batch, int in_c, int out_c, int h, int w, int out_h, int out_w, int kh, int kw, int stride_h, int stride_w, int dilation_h, int dilation_w, float* __restrict__ output) { const int TILE_H = 8; const int TILE_W = 32; const int OC_BLOCK = 32; int b = blockIdx.z / ((out_c + OC_BLOCK - 1) / OC_BLOCK); int oc_block = blockIdx.z % ((out_c + OC_BLOCK - 1) / OC_BLOCK); int oc_start = oc_block * OC_BLOCK; int oc_end = min(oc_start + OC_BLOCK, out_c); int oc_count = oc_end - oc_start; int tile_oh = blockIdx.y * TILE_H; int tile_ow = blockIdx.x * TILE_W; int local_ow = threadIdx.x; int local_oh = threadIdx.y; int tid = threadIdx.y * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; int oh = tile_oh + local_oh; int ow = tile_ow + local_ow; int smem_h = (TILE_H - 1) * stride_h + (kh - 1) * dilation_h + 1; int smem_w = (TILE_W - 1) * stride_w + (kw - 1) * dilation_w + 1; extern __shared__ float smem[]; float* smem_input = smem; float* smem_weight = smem + smem_h * smem_w; float acc[OC_BLOCK]; for (int i = 0; i < oc_count; i++) acc[i] = 0.0f; int in_h_start = tile_oh * stride_h; int in_w_start = tile_ow * stride_w; for (int ic = 0; ic < in_c; ic++) { // Load input tile int total_input = smem_h * smem_w; for (int idx = tid; idx < total_input; idx += blockDim.x * blockDim.y) { int ih_local = idx / smem_w; int iw_local = idx % smem_w; int global_ih = in_h_start + ih_local; int global_iw = in_w_start + iw_local; float val = 0.0f; if (global_ih < h && global_iw < w) { val = input[((b * in_c + ic) * h + global_ih) * w + global_iw]; } smem_input[ih_local * smem_w + iw_local] = val; } // Load weights int total_weight = oc_count * kh * kw; for (int idx = tid; idx < total_weight; idx += blockDim.x * blockDim.y) { int oci = idx / (kh * kw); int tmp = idx % (kh * kw); int k_h = tmp / kw; int k_w = tmp % kw; int global_oc = oc_start + oci; smem_weight[oci * kh * kw + tmp] = weight[((global_oc * in_c + ic) * kh + k_h) * kw + k_w]; } __syncthreads(); if (oh < out_h && ow < out_w) { int ih_base = (oh * stride_h) - in_h_start; int iw_base = (ow * stride_w) - in_w_start; for (int k_h = 0; k_h < kh; k_h++) { for (int k_w = 0; k_w < kw; k_w++) { int ih = ih_base + k_h * dilation_h; int iw = iw_base + k_w * dilation_w; float in_val = smem_input[ih * smem_w + iw]; for (int oci = 0; oci < oc_count; oci++) { acc[oci] += in_val * smem_weight[oci * kh * kw + k_h * kw + k_w]; } } } } __syncthreads(); } if (oh < out_h && ow < out_w) { for (int oci = 0; oci < oc_count; oci++) { int global_oc = oc_start + oci; output[((b * out_c + global_oc) * out_h + oh) * out_w + ow] = acc[oci]; } } } ``` Wait, does this handle padding? No, we pre-pad in Python. So `in_h_start = tile_oh * stride_h` assumes the padded input starts at the same coordinate. Since padding was applied, `oh` maps to `oh * stride_h` in the padded input. Correct. Host wrapper: ```cpp torch::Tensor conv2d_forward( torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor weight, int64_t batch, int64_t in_c, int64_t out_c, int64_t h, int64_t w, int64_t out_h, int64_t out_w, int64_t kh, int64_t kw, int64_t stride_h, int64_t stride_w, int64_t dilation_h, int64_t dilation_w) { auto output = torch::empty({batch, out_c, out_h, out_w}, input.options()); const int TILE_H = 8; const int TILE_W = 32; const int OC_BLOCK = 32; dim3 block(TILE_W, TILE_H); dim3 grid( (out_w + TILE_W - 1) / TILE_W, (out_h + TILE_H - 1) / TILE_H, batch * ((out_c + OC_BLOCK - 1) / OC_BLOCK) ); int smem_h = (TILE_H - 1) * stride_h + (kh - 1) * dilation_h + 1; int smem_w = (TILE_W - 1) * stride_w + (kw - 1) * dilation_w + 1; size_t smem_size = (smem_h * smem_w + OC_BLOCK * kh * kw) * sizeof(float); conv2d_kernel<<<grid, block, smem_size>>>( input.data_ptr<float>(), weight.data_ptr<float>(), batch, in_c, out_c, h, w, out_h, out_w, kh, kw, stride_h, stride_w, dilation_h, dilation_w, output.data_ptr<float>() ); return output; } ``` This is a clean design. Let's compile it. Wait, `cublas` or other libraries are not used. So we don't link against cublas unless needed. Great. I will also add `extra_cflags` and `extra_cuda_cflags` for optimization. Let's also consider whether I can use array-of-structs or struct-of-arrays for weights/data to improve memory coalescing. Weights are accessed by all threads simultaneously for different OC. So storing weights as `smem_weight[OC_BLOCK][KH][KW]` means `smem_weight[0][kh][kw]`, `smem_weight[1][kh][kw]`, etc., are adjacent in memory. When threads access `smem_weight[oci][kh][kw]` with different `oci` (since each thread computes 16 OCs, it accesses `oci` sequentially in a loop, not coalesced across threads). Actually, in the thread loop: ```cpp for (int oci = 0; oci < OC_BLOCK; oci++) { acc += in_val * smem_weight[oci][kh][kw]; } ``` Each thread reads `smem_weight[0..15][kh][kw]`. Different threads read the same `oci` at the same time but across `oci` they read different addresses. Since `oci` is in the inner loop, there is no bank conflict as long as the address pattern doesn't conflict. Shared memory banks are 32-way. `smem_weight[oci]` is spaced by 35 floats. float4? Actually on H100 shared memory has 32 banks. Address `oci * 35 * 4`. If 35*4 = 140 bytes. 140 / 4 = 35. Since 35 is odd, accesses across threads for a fixed `oci` won't conflict. But accesses for sequential `oci` might stride by 35 floats, which wraps around banks. Since 35 and 32 are coprime, the stride avoids bank conflicts! So reading `smem_weight[oci]` sequentially is actually very well bank-conflict free. This is a great property of choosing KH*KW as odd. So the kernel design is excellent. Kernel design: ```cpp #define TILE_H 16 #define TILE_W 16 #define OC_BLOCK 16 __global__ void conv2d_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ weight, float* __restrict__ output, int batch, int in_c, int out_c, int h, int w, int out_h, int out_w, int kh, int kw, int stride_h, int stride_w, int dilation_h, int dilation_w, int pad_h, int pad_w) { int b = blockIdx.z / ((out_c + OC_BLOCK - 1) / OC_BLOCK); int oc_block = blockIdx.z % ((out_c + OC_BLOCK - 1) / OC_BLOCK); int oc_start = oc_block * OC_BLOCK; int oc_end = min(oc_start + OC_BLOCK, out_c); int oc_count = oc_end - oc_start; int tile_oh = blockIdx.y * TILE_H; int tile_ow = blockIdx.x * TILE_W; int local_ow = threadIdx.x; int local_oh = threadIdx.y; int oh = tile_oh + local_oh; int ow = tile_ow + local_ow; // Each thread computes a 2x2 tile? No, let's make block 8x8 and each thread computes 2x2. // Better: block 8x8, tile 16x16. // So: int thread_oh = local_oh * 2; int thread_ow = local_ow * 2; // Wait, 8*2 = 16, good. int ohs[2], ows[2]; ohs[0] = tile_oh + thread_oh; ohs[1] = tile_oh + thread_oh + 1; ows[0] = tile_ow + thread_ow; ows[1] = tile_ow + thread_ow + 1; int smem_h = (TILE_H - 1) * stride_h + (kh - 1) * dilation_h + 1; int smem_w = (TILE_W - 1) * stride_w + (kw - 1) * dilation_w + 1; extern __shared__ float smem[]; float* smem_input = smem; // size smem_h * smem_w float* smem_weight = smem + smem_h * smem_w; // size OC_BLOCK * kh * kw float acc[2][2][OC_BLOCK]; // We must use only up to oc_count, but keep array at OC_BLOCK. #pragma unroll for(int i=0;i<2;i++) for(int j=0;j<2;j++) for(int k=0;k<OC_BLOCK;k++) acc[i][j][k] = 0.0f; int in_h_start = tile_oh * stride_h - pad_h; int in_w_start = tile_ow * stride_w - pad_w; for(int ic=0; ic<in_c; ic++) { // Cooperative load input int total_input = smem_h * smem_w; int tid = threadIdx.y * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; for(int idx=tid; idx<total_input; idx+=blockDim.x*blockDim.y) { int ih_local = idx / smem_w; int iw_local = idx % smem_w; int global_ih = in_h_start + ih_local; int global_iw = in_w_start + iw_local; float val = 0.0f; if(global_ih >= 0 && global_ih < h && global_iw >= 0 && global_iw < w) { val = input[((b * in_c + ic) * h + global_ih) * w + global_iw]; } smem_input[ih_local * smem_w + iw_local] = val; } // Cooperative load weight int total_weight = oc_count * kh * kw; for(int idx=tid; idx<total_weight; idx+=blockDim.x*blockDim.y) { int oci = idx / (kh * kw); int tmp = idx % (kh * kw); int k_h = tmp / kw; int k_w = tmp % kw; int global_oc = oc_start + oci; smem_weight[oci * kh * kw + tmp] = weight[((global_oc * in_c + ic) * kh + k_h) * kw + k_w]; } __syncthreads(); // Compute for 2x2 pixels #pragma unroll for(int i=0; i<2; i++) { int oh_pixel = ohs[i]; if(oh_pixel >= out_h) continue; #pragma unroll for(int j=0; j<2; j++) { int ow_pixel = ows[j]; if(ow_pixel >= out_w) continue; int ih_base = (oh_pixel * stride_h - pad_h) - in_h_start; int iw_base = (ow_pixel * stride_w - pad_w) - in_w_start; #pragma unroll for(int k_h=0; k_h<kh; k_h++) { #pragma unroll for(int k_w=0; k_w<kw; k_w++) { int ih = ih_base + k_h * dilation_h; int iw = iw_base + k_w * dilation_w; // Bounds check not needed because smem covers the footprint. float in_val = smem_input[ih * smem_w + iw]; #pragma unroll for(int oci=0; oci<oc_count; oci++) { acc[i][j][oci] += in_val * smem_weight[oci * kh * kw + k_h * kw + k_w]; } } } } } __syncthreads(); } // Write output #pragma unroll for(int i=0; i<2; i++) { int oh_pixel = ohs[i]; if(oh_pixel >= out_h) continue; #pragma unroll for(int j=0; j<2; j++) { int ow_pixel = ows[j]; if(ow_pixel >= out_w) continue; #pragma unroll for(int oci=0; oci<oc_count; oci++) { int global_oc = oc_start + oci; output[((b * out_c + global_oc) * out_h + oh_pixel) * out_w + ow_pixel] = acc[i][j][oci]; } } } } ``` Wait, I used `#pragma unroll` on `for(int k_h=0; k_h<kh; k_h++)`. Since `kh` and `kw` are not compile-time constants (passed as arguments), unrolling might not happen or might default to a small limit. In CUDA, `#pragma unroll` on a loop with unknown bounds might still unroll partially or not at all. It's often ignored. I can remove unroll on those. Also, weight indexing: `smem_weight[oci * kh * kw + k_h * kw + k_w]`. This creates a bank conflict? Let's analyze. In the inner loop: ```cpp for(int oci=0; oci<oc_count; oci++) { acc[i][j][oci] += in_val * smem_weight[...]; } ``` For a fixed thread at fixed `k_h, k_w`, it iterates over `oci`. Since `oci` varies, the addresses are spaced by `kh*kw` floats. If `kh*kw = 35`, 35*4=140 bytes. Bank index = (addr/4) % 32. (oci*35 + offset) % 32. Since 35 % 32 = 3, the bank index cycles with step 3. For sequential `oci`, consecutive reads hit banks (offset + 3*oci) % 32. This is stride 3, so in 32 banks, consecutive reads are in different banks. No bank conflict for a single thread. For multiple threads, each thread reads its own `oci` at different times ( sequential in the loop). There is no simultaneous access across threads for different `oci` in this loop. Since `oh = tile_oh + thread_oh + delta`, offset = `(thread_oh + delta) * stride_h`. Yes! Let's finalize ModelNew: ```python class ModelNew(torch.nn.Module): def __init__(self, in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size, stride=(1,1), padding=(0,0), dilation=(1,1), groups=1, bias=False): super().__init__() self.in_channels = in_channels self.out_channels = out_channels self.kernel_size = kernel_size self.stride = stride self.padding = padding self.dilation = dilation self.groups = groups assert out_channels % groups == 0 assert in_channels % groups == 0 self.weight = torch.nn.Parameter(torch.empty(out_channels, in_channels // groups, *kernel_size)) if bias: self.bias = torch.nn.Parameter(torch.empty(out_channels)) else: self.bias = None # init same as default torch.nn.init.kaiming_uniform_(self.weight, a=math.sqrt(5)) if self.bias is not None: fan_in = in_channels // groups * kernel_size[0] * kernel_size[1] bound = 1 / math.sqrt(fan_in) torch.nn.init.uniform_(self.bias, -bound, bound) def forward(self, x): # x: [B, in_c, H, W] # pad if necessary if self.padding[0] > 0 or self.padding[1] > 0: x = torch.nn.functional.pad(x, (self.padding[1], self.padding[1], self.padding[0], self.padding[0])) batch = x.size(0) h = x.size(2) w = x.size(3) kh, kw = self.kernel_size out_h = (h + 2*self.padding[0] - self.dilation[0]*(kh-1) - 1) // self.stride[0] + 1 out_w = (w + 2*self.padding[1] - self.dilation[1]*(kw-1) - 1) // self.stride[1] + 1 out = x.new_empty(batch, self.out_channels, out_h, out_w) in_c_per_group = self.in_channels // self.groups out_c_per_group = self.out_channels // self.groups for g in range(self.groups): x_g = x[:, g*in_c_per_group:(g+1)*in_c_per_group] w_g = self.weight[g*out_c_per_group:(g+1)*out_c_per_group] out_g = conv2d_module.conv2d_forward( x_g, w_g, batch, in_c_per_group, out_c_per_group, h, w, out_h, out_w, kh, kw, self.stride[0], self.stride[1], self.dilation[0], self.dilation[1], self.padding[0], self.padding[1] ) out[:, g*out_c_per_group:(g+1)*out_c_per_group] = out_g if self.bias is not None: out += self.bias.view(1, -1, 1, 1) return out ``` Wait, after padding, `h` and `w` change.
